<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Indigenous languages of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_America" title="Languages of North America">Languages of North America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_America" title="Languages of South America">Languages of South America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="691" data-file-width="624" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/220px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/330px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/440px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Languages spoken in the Americas</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Various <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a> are spoken in the Americas. Some are of European origin, others are spoken by indigenous peoples or are the mixture of various idioms like the different creoles.</p>
<p>The most widely spoken language in the Americas is Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> The dominant language of Latin America is Spanish, though the most populous nation in Latin America, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, speaks <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>. Small enclaves of French-, Dutch- and English-speaking regions also exist in Latin America, notably in <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, Suriname, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> respectively, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" title="Haitian Creole language">Haitian Creole</a>, of French origin, is dominant in the nation of <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>. <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Native languages</a> are more prominent in Latin America than in <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">Anglo-America</a>, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" title="Nahuatl language">Nahuatl</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" title="Guaraní language">Guaraní</a> as the most common. Various other native languages are spoken with less frequency across both Anglo-America and Latin America. <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">Creole languages</a> other than Haitian Creole are also spoken in parts of Latin America.</p>
<p>The dominant language of Anglo-America is English. French is also official in Canada, where it is the predominant language in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> and an official language in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> along with English. It is also an important language in <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, and in parts of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>. Spanish has kept an ongoing presence in the Southwestern United States, which formed part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">Viceroyalty of New Spain</a>, especially in <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, where <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_Spanish" title="New Mexican Spanish">a distinct variety of Spanish</a> spoken since the 17th century has survived. It has more recently become widely spoken in other parts of the United States due to heavy immigration from Latin America. High levels of immigration in general have brought great linguistic diversity to Anglo-America, with over 300 languages known to be spoken in the United States alone, but most languages are spoken only in small enclaves and by relatively small immigrant groups.</p>
<p>The nations of <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, Suriname, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> are generally considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2012)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> not to fall into either Anglo-America or Latin America due to lingual differences with Latin America, geographic differences with Anglo-America, and cultural and historical differences with both regions; English is the primary language of Guyana and Belize, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> is the official and written language of Suriname.</p>
<p>Most of the non-native languages have, to different degrees, evolved differently from the mother country, but are usually still mutually intelligible. Some have combined, however, which has even resulted in completely new languages, such as <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">Papiamento</a>, which is a combination of Portuguese, Spanish, Dutch (representing the respective colonizers), native <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a>, various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_languages" title="African languages">African languages</a>, and, more recently English. The <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> <a href="/wiki/Portu%C3%B1ol" title="Portuñol">Portuñol</a>, a mixture of Portuguese and Spanish, is spoken in the border regions of Brazil and neighboring Spanish-speaking countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> More specifically, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol_language" title="Riverense Portuñol language">Riverense Portuñol</a> is spoken by around 100,000 people in the border regions of Brazil and Uruguay. Due to <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>, there are many communities where other languages are spoken from all parts of the world, especially in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>—very important destinations for immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_(word)" title="American (word)">American (word)</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">Speakers of English</a> generally refer to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landmass" title="Landmass">landmasses</a> of North America and South America as <i>the Americas</i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a></i>, or the <i><a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> The adjective <i>American</i> may be used to indicate something pertains to the Americas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OEDAMERICAN_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-OEDAMERICAN-1">[1]</a></sup> but this term is primarily used in English to indicate something pertaining to the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OEDAMERICAN_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-OEDAMERICAN-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-145">[143]</a></sup> Some non-ambiguous alternatives exist, such as the adjective <i>Pan-American</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> or <i>New Worlder</i> as a demonym for a resident of the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED.7CNew_Worlder_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-OED.7CNew_Worlder-2">[2]</a></sup> Use of <i>America</i> in the hemispherical sense is sometimes retained, or can occur when translated from other languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_National_Olympic_Committees" title="Association of National Olympic Committees">Association of National Olympic Committees</a> (ANOC) in Paris maintains a single continental association for "America", represented by one of the five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_rings" title="Olympic rings">Olympic rings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>American linguist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.L._Mencken" title="H.L. Mencken">H.L. Mencken</a> said, " The Latin-Americans use Nortamericano in formal writing, but, save in Panama, prefer nicknames in colloquial speech."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mencken_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mencken-149">[147]</a></sup> To avoid "American" one can use constructed terms in their languages derived from "United States" or even "North America".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-145">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> In Canada, its southern neighbor is often referred to as "the United States", "the U.S.A.", or (informally) "the States", while U.S. citizens are generally referred to as "Americans".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_145-2"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-145">[143]</a></sup> Most Canadians resent being referred to as "Americans".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_145-3"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-145">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish">Spanish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spanish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Spanish, <i>América</i> is a single continent composed of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">subcontinents</a> of <i>Sudamérica</i> and <i>Norteamérica</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridge</a> of <i>Centroamérica</i>, and the islands of the <i><a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antillas</a></i>. <i>Americano</i> or <i>americana</i> in Spanish refers to a person from <i>América</i> in a similar way that <i>europeo</i> or <i>europea</i> refers to a person from <i>Europa</i>. The terms <i>sudamericano/a</i>, <i>centroamericano/a</i>, <i>antillano/a</i> and <i>norteamericano/a</i> can be used to more specifically refer to the location where a person may live.</p>
<p>Citizens of the United States of America are normally referred to by the term <i>estadounidense</i> (rough literal translation: "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Statesian" title="United Statesian">United Statesian</a>") instead of <i>americano</i> or <i>americana</i> which is discouraged,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norteamerica_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-norteamerica-152">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadosunidos_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-estadosunidos-153">[151]</a></sup> and the country's name itself is officially translated as <i>Estados Unidos de América</i> (United States of America), commonly abbreviated as <i>Estados Unidos</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadosunidos_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-estadosunidos-153">[151]</a></sup> Also, the term <i>norteamericano</i> (North American) may refer to a citizen of the United States. This term is primarily used to refer to citizens of the United States, and less commonly to those of other North American countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norteamerica_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-norteamerica-152">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese">Portuguese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Portuguese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Portuguese, <i><a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica" title="pt:América">América</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericaPortBE_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmericaPortBE-154">[152]</a></sup> is a single continent composed of <i>América do Sul</i> (South America), <i>América Central</i> (Central America) and <i>América do Norte</i> (North America).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericaME_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmericaME-155">[153]</a></sup> It can be ambiguous, as <i>América</i> can be used to refer to the United States of America, but is avoided in print and formal environments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EstadosUnidosIt_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-EstadosUnidosIt-156">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EstadosUnidosESPN_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-EstadosUnidosESPN-157">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French">French</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: French">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In French the word <i>américain</i> may be used for things relating to the Americas; however, similar to English, it is most often used for things relating to the United States. <i>Panaméricain</i> may be used as an adjective to refer to the Americas without ambiguity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> French speakers may use the noun <i>Amérique</i> to refer to the whole landmass as one continent, or two continents, <i>Amérique du Nord</i> and <i>Amérique du Sud</i>. In French, <i>Amérique</i> is also used to refer to the United States, making the term ambiguous. Similar to English usage, <i>les Amériques</i> or <i>des Amériques</i> is used to refer unambiguously to the Americas.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch">Dutch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dutch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Dutch, the word <i>Amerika</i> mostly refers to the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although the United States is equally often referred to as <i>de Verenigde Staten</i> ("the United States") or <i>de VS</i> ("the US"), <i>Amerika</i> relatively rarely refers to the Americas, but it is the only commonly used Dutch word for the Americas. This often leads to ambiguity; and to stress that something concerns the Americas as a whole, Dutch uses a combination, namely <i>Noord- en Zuid-Amerika</i> (North and South America).</p>
<p>Latin America is generally referred to as <i>Latijns Amerika</i> or <i>Midden-Amerika</i> for Central America.</p>
<p>The adjective <i>Amerikaans</i> is most often used for things or people relating to the United States. There are no alternative words to distinguish between things relating to the United States or to the Americas. Dutch uses the local alternative for things relating to elsewhere in the Americas, such as <i>Argentijns</i> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_people" title="Argentine people">Argentine</a>, etc.</p>

The name <i>America</i> first appeared on a map in 1507 by the German cartographer Martin Waldseemüller, referring to the area now called Brazil]. Since the 16c, a name of the western hemisphere, often in the plural <i>Americas</i> and more or less synonymous with <i>the New World</i>. Since the 18c, a name of the United States of America. The second sense is now primary in English: ... However, the term is open to uncertainties: ..."</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-estadosunidos-153"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-estadosunidos_153-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-estadosunidos_153-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a class="external text" href="http://buscon.rae.es/dpd/srv/search?id=4EWtRO1VZD6v7sHSpo" rel="nofollow"><i>Diccionario panhispánico de dudas: Estados Unidos</i></a>. Real Academia Española. 2005.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAmericas&amp;rft.btitle=Diccionario+panhisp%C3%A1nico+de+dudas%3A+Estados+Unidos&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbuscon.rae.es%2Fdpd%2Fsrv%2Fsearch%3Fid%3D4EWtRO1VZD6v7sHSpo&amp;rft.pub=Real+Academia+Espa%C3%B1ola&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> "debe evitarse el empleo de americano para referirse exclusivamente a los habitantes de los Estados Unidos" ("the use of the term <i>americano</i> referring exclusively to the United States inhabitants must be avoided")</span></li>
